Whether the steamer should be released first is requested from your bureau for advice." (The rest is omitted.) The Shipping Administration Bureau immediately sent an urgent telegram to the Qidong County authorities, requesting that the steamer be released first and transferred to Shanghai for handling. The county replied to the Shipping Administration Bureau by telegram, saying, "Director Peng of the Shipping Administration Bureau, your telegram is noted. The Baohua steamer has been released. Li Ming, Magistrate of Qidong County." However, at 9:00 PM last night, the Ping An Company stated that although they had been notified by the Shipping Administration Bureau that the Baohua steamer had been released, they had not yet received a telegram from the ship, so there was no confirmation whether it would arrive in Shanghai today.

Dispute Over the Demolition of Houses in Leyi Lane, French Concession 140

The owner failed to build a fence.

The tenants held a general meeting yesterday.

Regarding the houses in Leyi Lane, An'na Jin Road, Nanyang Bridge, French Concession, because the owner Jiang Hanzhai announced an increase in rent, which was unsuccessful, he demolished the houses for reconstruction, which was opposed by the tenants. The Leiyili rent collection department, the Dick Parker Land Department, declared that it would not force tenants to move out unreasonably. The owner's side has taken further steps to exert pressure, deciding to build a fence by force and ordering the tenants to move out. The day before yesterday, a large number of craftsmen were sent with bamboo materials to build the fence. When the tenants heard the news, they came out to stop them. When the owner's side saw the tenants stopping the fence construction, they reported to the Songshan Road Police Station, requesting them to send detectives to protect them. After receiving the report, the police station sent a deputy detective to inspect the area. Tenant representatives Wang Dekui, Li Yuting, and Tang Maijin stated the reasons to the detective, saying that regarding the demolition dispute in this lane, the tenants have already petitioned the court to request an injunction against fence construction and demolition, and that temporary dispositions have been granted. Before a legal solution is reached, the tenants have the right to reside. After hearing the statements of the representatives and reviewing the owner's fence construction permit, the detective found that it had expired and could not be applied, and immediately stopped the fence construction. The large number of craftsmen then took the bamboo materials away, so the fence construction failed the day before yesterday. The tenants were deeply grateful to the police chief for handling the matter impartially and stopping the fence construction.

Tenants' Meeting: The Yiye Lane branch of the Fourth District Branch of the Shanghai Second Special District Citizens' Association, fearing that the owner would come to build the fence again, convened an emergency general meeting of all tenants at the Municipal Association in the Anxin Temple at the junction of Baer Road at 8:00 PM the day before yesterday, in order to find a solution. All the tenants attended, and Dong Wenli and Tong Lizhang, members of the Fourth District Branch of the Municipal Association, and Wu Kaisheng and Zhu Dianqing, legal advisors and two major lawyers, attended the meeting. Wang Dekui was elected as chairman and Yu Jingqing as recorder. After the report was made, the following countermeasures were decided: 1. All stood up to express their determination to never move no matter what pressure is applied. 2. If the owner comes to build the fence again, all the male and female tenants will come out together to stop him. 3. If the owner forcibly builds the fence, cuts off water, and demolishes the houses, they will file a lawsuit according to law. 4. When the owner announced the rent increase, he started repairs, but after collecting the back rent, he suddenly rebuilt the houses, which is not in accordance with the law. They will collect evidence and proceed according to law. 5. Another date will be set, and all will go to the Party and government organs to hold a large-scale petition, requesting relief. The meeting adjourned after the discussion.

Municipal Government Investigation: After receiving the tenants' petition stating that the owner had gone back on his word, had not increased the rent, and had demolished the houses for reconstruction, requesting assistance and relief, the Shanghai Municipal Government appointed Sun Junchangxin to investigate the details of the lane some time ago. However, the tenants have not yet received a reply.

This matter is of great importance to both vehicle owners and rickshaw pullers, and they should pay attention and follow through to facilitate the process.

The Anti-Drug Campaign Is Being Carried Out Vigorously

Yet Some Still Dare to Manufacture Large Quantities 151

Arrest of One Leads to the Capture of Many

Seizure of Numerous Red Pills and Manufacturing Equipment

French Concession detectives Superintendent Lambert (transliteration), Chinese Inspector Li Yaolong, Deputy Detective Zhang Daorong, and private detectives Shen Jinshu and Liu Jinrong were patrolling the area around Avenue Edward VII yesterday morning. At 5 o'clock, while patrolling near the intersection of East Xinqiao Street on Avenue Edward VII, they noticed a man carrying three mooncake boxes, acting suspiciously and appearing flustered. They immediately stopped him for questioning. Upon opening the boxes, they found red pills concealed inside, totaling three bags, or 3,000 pills. They brought him to the police station. The man confessed his name was Zhu Renzu (30 years old, from Wuxi, residing at 53 Zhihe Road, Chinese territory). He said he had purchased the red pills from Jin Cai (29 years old, local), who lived in the attic on the third floor of 116 East Xinqiao Street, and intended to sell them in the Chinese territory. The detectives immediately rushed to 116 East Xinqiao Street, arrested Jin Cai, and found eight bags of red pills, totaling 8,000 pills, in the makeup loft. Jin confessed that the red pills were delivered by Li Fengxiang (28 years old, from Nanjing), who lived at 3 Baolong Lane, Huaizhen Street, Nine Acres, in the city. The detectives took Jin and the red pills to the police station and then, together with police detectives from the Second District, First Precinct of the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau, secretly went to the address and arrested Li Fengxiang. He was brought to the bureau for questioning, where he confessed that the red pills were manufactured in a workshop operated by Chen Aqing (30 years old, from Ningbo) on the second floor of 122 Route Cardinal Mercier. They then detained Li in the Public Security Bureau and reported to the head of detectives, who rushed to 123 Route Cardinal Mercier and arrested Chen Aqing. Chen confessed that the workshop was located on the third floor of the front building of the home of Zhang Rongji (30 years old, from Ningbo) and Zhang Chenshi (28 years old), a married couple, at 11 Xiaoyou Lane, 26 Luban Road. The detectives then went to Xiaoyou Lane on Luban Road and arrested Zhang Rongji and Zhang Chenshi. They found five bags of finished red pills, totaling 5,000 pills, and an oven containing three trays of red pills being baked. They also seized 12 pounds of raw materials and manufacturing equipment. When questioned, the Zhang couple said that Chen Aqing was the mastermind. They then brought the seized goods and the individuals to the police station for joint investigation. At noon, the police station transferred Zhu Renzu, Jin Cai, Chen Aqing, Zhang Rongji, and Lu Chenshi to the First Criminal Division of the Second Special District Court. Presiding Judge Wang Gangxu convened the trial. Police lawyer Yao Zhaodi stated that the police station still needed to conduct a detailed investigation and that Li Fengxiang, who was detained in the Public Security Bureau, had not yet been brought in. He requested a ten-day extension to investigate the case and file a complaint. Private detective Shen Jinshu then reported on the case. The court verified the warrants, briefly questioned the defendants, and then granted the request for an extension to investigate further. The defendants were remanded in custody.

Discovery of Japanese Crew Member Smuggling Drugs on the Qingdao Maru 153

According to the Japanese newspaper *Mainichi Shimbun*, at 5 PM on the 1st, Chinese customs officers discovered that a steward, Yoshida Sueo, was smuggling heroin on the Dalian steamer Qingdao Maru. They immediately telegraphed the Japanese Consulate General's Police Department, who extradited the suspect. After a serious interrogation, Yoshida confessed that he had been working on the ship since 1930 and had become acquainted with the owner of Abe Pharmacy in Higashitomimachi, Dalian. On August 12th of this year, he smuggled two packages of heroin, each weighing one pound, with an estimated profit of 12.5 yuan per package, to Qingdao for delivery. When he arrived in Qingdao on August 13th, a woman personally came to pick them up, and he handed over the 25 yuan profit. On August 28th, at Abe Pharmacy, he was again entrusted with smuggling two packages of heroin under the same conditions, originally scheduled to be delivered to a woman when he went to Qingdao on August 31st. Because she did not come to the ship, he had no choice but to put them in the luggage warehouse for first-class passengers, and they were discovered by customs officers.

Joint Transportation Measures for Passengers on the Beijing-Shanghai, Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo, and Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railways 154

Connecting Station for Both Lines: Nanxingqiao Station

Connecting Station for Zhejiang-Jiangxi Line: Sanlangmiao Station

The Beijing-Shanghai, Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo, and Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railways have jointly agreed on the following measures for passenger transportation: Article 1. The Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administration (referred to as Line A) and the Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway Bureau (referred to as Line B) will jointly handle passenger transportation. In addition to complying with the domestic joint transportation regulations and passenger vehicle transportation regulations promulgated by the Ministry, these measures will be followed. Article 2. Joint Transportation Stations: In addition to the stations handling domestic passenger joint transportation, the Southern Shanghai Station and Gonghuan Bridge Station of Line A are added. Article 3. Joint Transportation Business: In accordance with the scope of domestic passenger joint transportation regulations, the business of fourth-class combined joint transportation tickets from Shanghai North Station, Shanghai South Station, Songjiang, Jiaxing, Haining, and Changan of Line A, and to and from the aforementioned stations, and third-class combined joint transportation tickets of Line B will be added. Article 4. Connecting Station: Nanxingqiao Station for Line A and Sanlangmiao Station for Line B. Article 5. Joint transportation passengers should be guided by the Nanxingqiao Station of Line A to the Sanlangmiao Station of Line B, and the latter station should take care of the transition. Article 6. Joint transportation of luggage, parcels, and miscellaneous items transported by passenger vehicles should be transported from Nanxingqiao Station of Line A to Sanlangmiao Station of Line B. Those transported from Line B to Line A should be transported from Sanlangmiao Station of Line B to Nanxingqiao Station of Line A for handover. Article 7. The cost of labor for transporting joint transportation luggage, parcels, and miscellaneous items between Nanxingqiao Station of Line A and Sanlangmiao Station of Line B should be shared by both lines in proportion to the joint transportation revenue. Article 8. The joint transportation management matters stipulated in these measures should be handled by the liquidation section of the Railway Joint Transportation Office. Article 9. If there are any matters not covered in these measures, Line A and Line B may consult and amend them at any time.

Each Bill Is a One-Yuan Note

Qiu Qinghang Discovered to Have Embezzled 50,000 Yuan 160

10,000 Yuan Falsely Recorded as 60,000 Yuan

Crime Location Presents Jurisdictional Issue

Qiu Qinghang, from Hangzhou, currently resides at 7 Deshun Lane, Muir Road. In 1930, he was appointed by the Shanghai Four Banks Savings Association as the manager of the Xiamen branch. While in office, Qiu deposited one thousand silver dollars with the Chung Nan Bank in the name of the branch, but recorded a deposit of sixty thousand silver dollars in the ledgers. Qiu embezzled a total of fifty thousand silver dollars from it. In August of this year, the Shanghai headquarters transferred Qiu to Shanghai to handle matters and appointed a Mr. Huang to take over. After taking over, Mr. Huang checked the accounts and discovered Qiu's embezzlement. He telegraphed the headquarters, who reported it to the Chief Police Station. Detectives were ordered to arrest Qiu on the previous day and bring him back to the police station for detention. Yesterday morning, he was escorted to the First Criminal Division of the First District Court. Police lawyer Jiang Baolian stated the case, prosecuting him for occupational embezzlement under Article 357 of the Criminal Law. When questioned, Qiu Qinghang's confession was evasive. Judge Feng Shide stated that the crime was committed in Xiamen, and the court had no jurisdiction and should transfer it to the Shanghai District Court. Police lawyer Jiang requested a temporary stay of the ruling for a few days, pending the Municipal Council's review of whether the jurisdiction was incorrect before deciding whether to transfer it. The court granted the request and ordered a postponement for two days for further interrogation.

Extortion Case in the Gutter 161

No One Retrieved the Money, Money Is Now Gone

Clue Found in the Drain

Tang Naijia, a Cantonese resident living at 246 Route Doumer, suddenly received several threatening letters from gangsters between the 15th and 29th of last month. Initially, they demanded 1,000 yuan, and then reduced the amount to a minimum of 500 yuan. They arranged for the money to be wrapped in paper and placed in a drain next to 451 Jiangxi Road around 2 PM the day before yesterday. Someone would retrieve it, or they would take drastic measures. He reported the situation to the D'Estaing Road Police Station, who dispatched Chinese Detective Fan Defu and Detective Liu Decheng, along with his nephew Tang Jin, with six silver dollars in real currency and the rest filled with ghost money, carefully wrapped and secretly went to the location on time, scattering to observe the situation. Until after 4 PM, no one arrived. The detectives inspected the original site and found that the package was gone. They were very surprised. They saw that there was a hole in the drain connecting to the house at 451 (which is a printing office). They went inside and found a worker named Ji Zhongming, from Haimen, who used to work as a tea servant at the victim's place. He was arrested and confessed that his father had done this and taken the package. He was brought to the police station. Yesterday morning, he was escorted to the Third Criminal Division of the First District Court. Municipal Council lawyer Li Zhishan recounted the events. When questioned, the defendant's confession was evasive. Judge Xiao Yucheng ordered a postponement for further investigation and review.

Large Turtle Discovered on the Wusong Beach 162

Turtle Shell Has the Tianqi Reign Year

Likely an Item From Hundreds of Years Ago

Yesterday morning, a turtle as large as a round table washed up on the beach in front of the seaside park at the eastern end of Wusong Outer Bund. A rickshaw puller spotted it and managed to retrieve it to the beach. However, the turtle had already died. Four people then carried it ashore and brought it into the rickshaw puller's shed. For a time, crowds gathered to watch the enormous creature. It is said that the Tianqi reign year and the words "Peng's Release" are engraved on the turtle's back. Experts know that the turtle is from the Ming Dynasty.

Lawyer Zhu Kuangming Accuses Lawyer Gu Jirong of Extortion and Fraud 163

Stemming from a Debt Dispute Between Tao Shangen and Another Person

Gu and His Secretary Ji Chao Allegedly Forced Zhu to Settle

Lawyer Zhu Kuangming filed a criminal self-accusation with the First Special District Local Court against lawyer Gu Jirong, Tao Shangen (director of the China-Asia Machinery Company), and Ji Chao (formerly a legal secretary), accusing them of extortion and fraud. The court has repeatedly summoned them for questioning. However, due to the defendants' request for a possible settlement and the unavailability of many witnesses, no questioning took place. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Zhan Liangce held another hearing. Both the plaintiff and the defendants arrived with their respective lawyers. First, the plaintiff, Zhu Kuangming, stated the facts of the accusation, roughly as follows: The defendant Tao Shangen was involved in a debt dispute with Pan and Xie. Gu Jirong represented Tao, while I was entrusted by Xie. Later, the case was decided in the third instance, and Pan and others lost. Pan had already fled to the Chinese-controlled area. This court requested the Shanghai Local Court to assist in detaining Pan for enforcement. At that time, Pan sent a letter to Tao, stating that the case had already been settled through mediation and that the appeals in the second and third instances were not at his initiative. After reading Pan's letter, Tao suspected that I, as the representative of the defendant Xie Tiancheng, was responsible for initiating the second and third appeals. Coincidentally, Tao's friend, surnamed Xu, also saw Pan's letter and encouraged Tao to sue me for forging documents in the Shanghai Local Court. The lawyer representing Tao in the lawsuit was the defendant Gu Jirong. After they filed the lawsuit, Gu Jirong repeatedly called me, urging me to settle. I strongly believed in resolving the matter through legal means, so I refused. On August 9th, the defendant Ji Chao came to my office, claiming to represent Gu Jirong and wanting to discuss the matter with me, but I still refused. Then, on August 21st, Gu and Tao came again, insisting that I pay for a settlement, with many threatening words. Gu Jirong even drafted a settlement agreement at the time, which I asked to see and then kept. Gu and others panicked and asked me to return it. They pestered me from 11 a.m. to 2 p.m., refusing to leave. I was angry at their rudeness and warned them that if they continued to linger, I would report them to the police. Gu, realizing he was in the wrong and feeling guilty, left first but ordered Tao to continue demanding the draft from me. I then reported to the Central Police Station. The entire process can be verified by investigating with the Central Police Station, which will prove the defendants' extortion and fraud. When questioned, the defendant Gu Jirong stated that he was unaware that Tao Shangen had sued Zhu in the Shanghai Local Court and did not represent him. He also denied calling Zhu to discuss the matter. He only mentioned that before Tao sued Zhu, Zhu had talked about it, but Zhu came to his office on his own. The settlement draft was also prepared in his office, and there were witnesses who could be summoned to testify. Tao Shangen denied being with Gu Jirong at Zhu Kuangming's office on August 23rd, saying that he went to Suzhou on August 22nd and returned to Shanghai on the 24th, with postal correspondence as proof. He also stated that suing Zhu for forging documents was his own initiative and that no one else encouraged him. Ji Chao stated that he knew both lawyers Gu and Zhu. He had been Gu's secretary for many years. On July 28th, he received a call from Zhu, asking him to mediate the case in which Tao was suing him, but he immediately refused. Judge Zhan stated that the case still required investigation and ordered a continuance for further questioning and summoning of witnesses.

Suspended Chinese Constable Commits Suicide 164

Due to Financial Difficulties

Shi Xingzhao, from Chongming, was 31 years old and lived at No. 3 Songshou Lane, Xinzha Road. He was formerly a Chinese constable No. 303 in the Huishi Police Station and had been suspended for more than two months, leading to extreme financial difficulties. Overwhelmed with distress, he became despondent. On the evening of the day before yesterday, around 9 p.m., he went alone to the Qinghe Hotel at No. 6 Lane 118, Zhejiang Road, and secretly swallowed opium in room 227 to commit suicide. At 5 a.m. the next morning, the hotel tea server Gu Bingzhang discovered him and immediately reported to the Laozha Police Station, which dispatched Chinese Detective Li Shugui to investigate. He was rushed to Renji Hospital but died despite medical treatment. Three suicide notes were found on his person, stating that after losing his job, he struggled to make a living and faced extreme financial hardship, leading him to take this drastic measure. The detective had the body taken to the Fielun Road morgue. Yesterday morning, the First Special District Local Court sent Prosecutor Tang, along with forensic doctor Zhang Yan and clerk Wang Zuyi, to the morgue to verify the body. They confirmed that the deceased was indeed Shi Xingzhao, male, and that he had died from poisoning. The body was released to his uncle, Shi Zhijun, who signed a statement to take it back for coffin preparation.

Four Banks Preparation Treasury Issues Preparation Report 178

248th Time

The Four Banks Preparation Treasury is jointly established by the Yanye, Jincheng, Zhongnan, and Dalu Banks and specializes in the issuance of Zhongnan Bank banknotes. Reading Q&A

From Essays to the Sun Yat-sen Cultural Education Center Quarterly 189

Reading Guidance...

I heard someone say that this year is the year of magazines. Whether it is literary works or theoretical works, single books are always rarely published, and even if they are published, they cannot be sold. Only magazines are flooding the publishing world like a flood. Yes, I also feel that this is the case, but I think the current situation seems to be even more extreme. Instead of calling it the year of magazines, it seems more appropriate to call it the year of essays. You see, even magazines, those that are thicker and more rigid, are rarely published anywhere. Aren't all the things that can really be widely popular essay publications? This is probably the trend of the general reading world. Is this trend good? Personally, I still hope to read more systematic things. Fragmented reading makes it impossible to grasp the center of a thought. I don't think there is much benefit. Although short and concise essays are sometimes very enjoyable to read, they don't seem suitable for serious study. Is my opinion wrong?

Perhaps it is because of such a prejudice? Among recent publications, I am most happy to read the Sun Yat-sen Cultural Education Center Quarterly, because there are several very systematic and practical articles inside. The ones we think are most valuable are "The Trend of World Thought," "A Review of Soviet Russian Philosophical Thought," and "The Trend of World Politics." These articles use very simple explanations and very concise writing to give us a miniature of the current world cultural and political situation, which is of great help to us when we want to understand other individual issues in the future, so I have discussed each article very carefully. But my own judgment is very weak. I only think that everything they say is reasonable and correct. I don't know if there is anything wrong or that needs to be criticized. I hope you will also criticize these articles. If there is anything inappropriate, please point it out, so that we can get more benefits.

Lin Jun's letter

The situation in the publishing world that Mr. Lin said is real. Essays have become the darling of the current publishing world, that is, the darling of the general reading world, because if the reading world does not welcome them, the bookstore owners will never be so happy to publish them. From the perspective of reading benefits, it is easy to fall into low-level tastes to only talk about essays excessively, especially shallow and boring essays, and the result is of course not good. But good essays can cleverly expose and criticize the ills of social reality. After reading them, we can recognize many dark sides of social reality. Sometimes, even the long and lengthy articles do not pay attention to the things that can be seen clearly, which is the benefit of essays, that is, the place where essays are worth talking about. Of course, we cannot only know how to read essays because essays have this advantage. Essays, because they are short, can only grasp one aspect of the conversation and cannot take care of the overall situation of things. When reading essays, if you do not have a foundation in your own thoughts, you will often be led into a very narrow consciousness, clinging to one aspect of the truth, and unable to recognize the changes in righteousness, which is very dangerous. Therefore, essays cannot be taken to talk about exclusively. Talking about essays must first study solid theories, so that thoughts have assurance and are systematic, so as not to be harmed. From this point of view, we are very sympathetic to Mr. Lin's dissatisfaction with the current trend in the publishing world that places too much emphasis on essays. Our cultural world is still very young, and we still need more theoretical and solid masterpieces. (To be continued)

Chunqiu

Little Western Paradise 190

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter Two: The People Traveling in Business Return Home to Yongshou to Bid Farewell, the Great Monk Arrives in Chang'an

The child's father was already the third generation to come to Gansu. Unfortunately, in 1929, he was forced by military officers to join the army and was taken to Xi'an. Two women, one middle-aged and old, and the other who was in her prime, also became middle-aged, and the little girl also grew up. They thought that it was not a solution to continue like this. Gansu was very bitter, and the people who cultivated the land could not eat their fill, let alone a family of three women, so they abandoned their home and came to Xi'an. They said... even if they couldn't find the child's father, the child's uncle was an actor, and it was said that he was also in Xi'an, and maybe they could find him. Even if they couldn't find him again, they were willing to give the girl away. The dowry would not be collected, as long as they could settle the two older women, and they would be willing to be the third or fourth concubine. Old Li, do you think this is a good thing to hear? Unfortunately, I am a guest and cannot stay for a long time, otherwise, why not do such a cheap thing? Li Shilian smiled... You have inquired so clearly, you probably really have this intention. Jia Duocai said... I really didn't expect that such a good girl would come out of that poor place. His long blue floral cloth jacket, red and white face, and two white ear circles on his ears, of course, this is not platinum. Because it is not gold, it can be seen that this child also fits that sentence, love is natural. Alas! This impression is too deep for me. Saying that, he picked up the wine pot and poured a cup of wine, holding the cup directly to the tip of his nose. Putting down the wine cup, he picked up the chopsticks and just kept poking at the vegetables in the bowl, still shaking his head and savoring the beauty he had seen. Li Shilian smiled... That's right, this person is not bad. Jia Duocai said... Your words are so blindly agreeable and extremely boring. How do you know that the girl looks good? Li Shilian said... I have a message that I haven't told you yet. Guess where I went to my wife's place today. While saying that, he shook his head a few times, showing his smug expression. (31)

Remembering a Talented Ballad Singer 191

— Yi Sheng

As the saying goes... "Every profession produces a champion." To drop a word of literature, it is called... "No land, no talent." Storytellers in the past, because they relied on a mouth to exchange for food, traveled around the world for many years, and were called by the public "Jianghu friends who eat empty meals." They do not have a high social status in society. However, everything cannot be generalized. Old book listeners will not know that there was a famous ballad singer Ma Rufei in the late Qing Dynasty. The Pearl Pagoda that people sing today is a script that has been modified by him, so it is particularly elegant and interesting. I am afraid that few people know that he has the talent of an unattainable artist. I will describe an anecdote of his, which I heard from my father when I was a child.

Our hometown is Luodian Town, which belongs to Baoshan County. Every New Year in the town, there are very grand so-called horse lanterns held, (called out horse lanterns) which must parade every night from New Year's Day to the Lantern Festival; the owners of teahouses also hired storytellers to perform art and entertain guests, as an exciting event to decorate the New Year. Across from my house, there happened to be an old house with a spacious and dilapidated hall inside, which was setting up a teahouse. In a certain New Year, the neighboring teahouse also invited a storyteller, Ma Rufei. On the first night he took the stage, not long after he started telling the story, just as his spirit was gradually coming, suddenly the noisy gongs and drums sounded closer and closer; the tea guests in the hall knew that the horse lantern was coming, and went out of the hall in a swarm to watch the lantern along the street. Only Mr. Ma, who was sitting alone on the stage, was left in the hall. He could not help but be greatly disappointed. Helplessly, he had to stand on tiptoe and follow the crowd to look at the grand scene of the horse lantern outside the door, and felt that it was indeed "lantern shows are everywhere, and each has its own ingenuity." After a long time, the meeting finally ended, and the tea guests returned to their seats one after another, seemingly having eaten bear paws, and turned back to wait for the appearance of eating fish. Unexpectedly, Mr. Ma was not in a hurry to continue telling the story that had been interrupted, but he straightened the three-stringed lute, cleared his throat, and re-opened the "Horse Lantern Fu" like he was reciting it from memory, describing the ranks of the lantern meeting that had just passed in front of the door, and the various shows that were mixed together, from beginning to end in order, without any reversal or omission, and in a vivid manner. The audience all felt that the lantern meeting that had just passed was like the taste of fish, and the lantern meeting Fu that they heard at this time was like the taste of bear paws. In the sound of singing a sentence and drinking a full applause, the opening ended and the scheduled time for storytelling had passed. With such talent, compared to the ancients Cao Zijian's seven-step poem, he could only make a four-sentence seven-character poem on the spot, and there was no such a long piece that resembled the ancient style, and he had a particularly good memory, and it was really cute to talk about!

Biography of Mr. Jiang 193

— Drunken Chi Sheng

I have a friend, his surname is a homonym for "jiang" (stiff, rigid). Moreover, his temperament is stiff, and his situation is also stiff. Calling him "Mr. Jiang" is really accurate and unwavering, and even a little pitiful.

Mr. Jiang is from Shaoxing... He was born with a stiff nature. His old wife had passed away long ago, and he did not remarry, nor did he have any children. He lived alone at sea, relying on teaching to make a living. Wearing old optical glasses, he specialized in poetry, saying that it was a pure old scholar. When he walked, he walked in a straight line, and his body was straight and stiff. When he spoke, he was not sloppy, and he was sixty-four. If someone told him a few jokes, he would sit upright and say... "A child cannot be taught, I and you, stop at painting." A certain family in front asked him to sit in the mansion. Because the location was narrow, they asked him to sleep in the attic. He thought that the name of the attic gentleman was not elegant, and he was angry and said... "A scholar can be killed, but not humiliated. Is this tolerable, which is not tolerable." He left without saying goodbye, and his stiffness was so great!

Mr. Jiang has a long history in the bustling Shanghai. As the saying goes... "A tree is thousands of feet high, and the leaves fall back to its roots." He felt old and sick, so he missed his hometown in the face of the bright moon, and he had a great ambition to return. He also made a few seven-law poems, and told his relatives and friends everywhere. It is said that it is a farewell message, and it can also be regarded as a false expression of distress. Unexpectedly, after a few months, someone saw him still pacing on the road. He asked... "The fields are about to be deserted, why don't you go back?" He hesitated and replied... "Going back will eventually go back, but the schedule has not been set." Later, people realized that he wanted to go but stopped, and there was really an unavoidable reason. Originally, he had always been thrifty and self-sustaining, really so-called "a mustard seed is not given to others". Therefore, he has accumulated several thousand dollars in tuition fees over the years. If he took this money back, it would be like "returning home in brocade". It is inevitable that it will arouse the covetousness of the clan, which is really a bit dangerous. Moreover, this is the crystallization of his hard work, and it is by no means his wish to give it away in the future. Therefore, he was full of hesitation, and could not return. He still lived under the eaves of others, spending his lonely and monotonous life. Sometimes he sighed and said... "A person without money is certainly going to be stiff. I have a few dollars, and I have become very stiff. Why, why, I will be Mr. Jiang for the rest of my life." His personal destination and the disposal of money have become stiff him. In the end, there is no way to solve it!

Record of Misty Fragrance 194

— Originally written by Princess Deling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

The hearts of our group of people also increased with infinite pleasure... The farther we were from the noisy, strict, and terrifying city of Beijing, the more excited and happier we were, and no one wanted to think about the situation after returning in the future.

"Ah! Spring is really the most lovely season of the year!" A piece of spring in the air seemed to have given the Empress Dowager a considerable influence; one day, she suddenly sighed to me... "In this kind of weather, people really seem to be back to their youth! Spring originally belongs to young people!"

Then, she recited a poem by the great Tang Dynasty poet Li Bai, "Spring Dawn," in a very beautiful tone...

"I sleep soundly in spring, not aware of dawn,

Birds are singing here and there.

I heard the sound of wind and rain last night,

I wonder how many flowers have fallen!"

The Empress Dowager had a considerable appreciation for poetry... Although I had never seen her write any poems myself, I often heard her recite ancient poems. Among the many great poets of ancient China, the one she admired the most was Li Bai. She had read almost all of the poems written by Li Bai, or it could be said that she could recite them all. Because the Empress Dowager loved Li's poems so much, it created a trend. At that time, a group of literati in the court almost all strived to imitate Li Bai's style... Occasionally, if the Empress Dowager saw it, they would casually praise a sentence or two, and these people would be as happy as if they had received some kind of honor, and from then on they would be self-appointed and think that they could really follow in the footsteps of Qinglian. In fact, the Empress Dowager's poetry was also very shallow, but she did have some research on Chinese ancient history and those more famous unofficial histories or legends, which was beyond the reach of ordinary people. (141)

Odds and Ends

Beehive 195

— Jin Xiong Yu

The beehive is named because its partitions resemble rooms; bees are generally divided into three types, namely honey bees, black bees (commonly known as iron-headed bees), and wasps (commonly known as long-legged bees). Honey bees are mostly domesticated, used to make honey, which is used in various medicines or as food. The wide range of uses makes beekeepers live by it. Black bees live in wooden caves, so they are found between old houses and old trees, which is where they gather. Only wasps can build nests, mostly in the woods. The construction takes time, and the shape is very peculiar. In my garden, there is a white bark pine tree that is more than 200 years old. The branches and trunks are lush and can be embraced, making it the crown of my county. One year, it was blown down by a strong wind, and then supported with wood, so its branches and leaves are not very high. One day, as the sunset was setting, I was talking and sitting under the tree with two or three confidants, and I saw a beehive above, with more than ten wasps attached to it. Someone said that it stings people, please remove it. I quietly loved it, and said slowly: "I saw it at the beginning, starting with one bee, hugging the tree branch, cursing the glue foam as a tie, initially like a thorn, gradually like a mushroom, now like a cup, one room is formed, then one child is born, those who are sleeping with feathers drooping are all born by one bee. The common people start with the land of a cone, combing the wind and bathing the rain, working day and night, fortunately they have built a small house to gather their children and grandchildren. Once a strong violence suddenly rises and robs it, even those who can bear it, when they hear it, sigh and have a sad color. I would like to be sad for those who are sad for the people, and to be sad for things. You wait quietly, don't be noisy, even if our group gathers below, the bees will come from and go by themselves, and will never sting each other, because the poison of the world is in the heart, and the poison of the bee is only in the tail." Everyone nodded, and I led them to look closely, without being surprised. I slightly shook it with grass, and some flew away without stopping, and some gathered on my clothes, without any intention of stinging people. Gentlemen, please observe the beehive's place, which is sticky like glue, and the wind and rain cannot defeat it, otherwise it will not be able to defeat the group of bees. Now it is as big as a plate.

Ant Army 196

The character for ant was originally written as 螘, and their colors are red, black, and a yellowish-red; their bodies are divided into three parts: head, thorax, and abdomen. Mountain ants and large black ants are about four to five fen in length, while small ants are about one fen in length. Although their shapes and bodies are small, they like to be united and are fond of fighting. Those of the same kind gather together to live, and there are hundreds to thousands in a nest. The internal governance is also well-organized, such as the queen ant and the male ant who specialize in reproduction, worker ants who are in charge of internal work, and worker ants who forage for food and soldier ants who are in charge of battle. When they go out to find food, observing their actions, they are single-minded and do not slacken at all. When they get a drop of food, they return to the nest and do not act selfishly. If they encounter a large amount of food that they cannot carry alone, they will quickly run back to the nest to report to their fellows. Before long, they will form a team and arrive excitedly. Seeing the target object, they do their best to drag it back together. If they encounter another tribe fighting for food, they will fight bravely and solemnly, not hesitating to sacrifice themselves, as if they have discipline. Therefore, they go forward bravely. If there are those who die in battle or are wounded, several ants will be seen dragging them back cooperatively, never abandoning them. Therefore, it is indeed worthwhile to stop and watch them. Ants are tiny insects, but their solidarity, love, wisdom, bravery in fighting, and loyalty in everything are praised by people. Once, I witnessed an even more interesting spectacle, so I will describe it to tell the readers: One evening, I was walking in the courtyard. At that time, crows were flying around and singing loudly as they returned to their nests. Crickets chirped in the shadows of the walls. There were several rose bushes here, and the flowers were in full bloom, red and white, beautiful and dazzling. Hundreds of ants gathered under the flowers. Moved by curiosity, I bent down to look and saw the ants fighting fiercely with a single-winged butterfly. Although many fell, those rushing forward did not stop. Soon, the butterfly's wings were completely broken, and it could not fly. It sometimes bowed and sometimes looked up, staggering. Behind it, hundreds of ant soldiers chased after it urgently. The vanguard ants had already caught up and jumped onto the butterfly's back. The butterfly immediately turned its head and bit them to death, abandoning the corpses. The second and third ants arrived one after another, and the momentum became more urgent. The butterfly turned its head and bit them to death as before, and dozens of corpses lay there. At that time, the butterfly was already exhausted and gradually unable to support itself. The ant army took the opportunity to press forward. At this critical moment, the butterfly quickly moved forward to reach the stem of a grass, climbed up the long leaves, and held on to the dangerous terrain to defend itself. Those who forced their way forward were still bitten to death, and none of them returned alive. The place where the butterfly defended was narrow and dangerous, only allowing one ant to pass. The butterfly had no worries about being attacked from behind, nor was it troubled by running around. Its courage was tenfold, and many ants died, but they could not defeat the butterfly. Then, the ant army was seen retreating together, gathering in one place, and whispering to each other, as if discussing something. After the discussion, they reorganized their ranks and gathered under the roots of the grass, working together to bite off the leaves. The leaves fell and the butterfly fell. The ant army gathered from all sides, and in less than a moment, the butterfly was killed. The ants then carried the butterfly's corpse and returned in triumph.

Datong University Invites Chen Boming to Lecture on Boming Musical Notation 211

Held every night from 7 to 9 PM this week, Monday, Tuesday, Thursday, and Friday. Chen Boming, former professor of Jinan University and currently serving in the Political Training Department of the Military Commission, has invented the "Boming Musical Notation" after more than ten years of dedicated research. It can use the simplest musical notation to translate our country's characters and local dialects, as well as the characters of dozens of countries in Europe, America, and Japan. The rhyme is exceptionally accurate, and the spelling is extremely simple. Since its invention, it has been promoted in schools in the Northwest, Henan, Luoyang, the capital, and in the troops of the 87th Division and the First Army, with remarkable results. Datong University in this city has always paid close attention to new discoveries in Chinese and foreign academic circles. Admiring the perfection of the "Boming Musical Notation," the university specially invited the inventor of the musical notation, Chen Boming, to come to the school to give a lecture on the 21st of last month, so that students could study extracurricular academics. Recently, Dean Tai of the School of Education of the university, because the students of the school were very interested in this kind of linguistic invention, specially negotiated with Mr. Chen and agreed to invite Mr. Chen to come to the school to give a detailed lecture every night from 7 to 9 PM this week, Monday, Tuesday, Thursday, and Friday, in order to practice. Last night was the first night, and the number of students participating in the study of the musical notation exceeded the number of sign-ups by more than double, reaching more than 90 people.

My Humble Opinion on Implementing Production Education (I) Wang Gongxia Quick Record 213

Director of the Education Bureau, Pan Gongzhan, delivered a speech at the Members' Congress of the Third District Education Association of this city.

Chairman, comrades, today is the Members' Congress of the Third District Education Association of this city. I am invited to say a few words. I am very happy to be able to take this opportunity to share some of my recent thoughts on education with you all.

In the past year or two, especially this year, you have probably seen many criticisms of education in newspapers, magazines, or other books. Because the national crisis is getting heavier day by day, and the world situation is getting more dangerous day by day, everyone feels that the education cause is also becoming more urgent day by day. And we, who serve in the great education circles, whether we are education administrative organs or people in schools, are also taking on more and more important responsibilities. Generally speaking, you all know where these many criticisms are pointing. Why is there a national crisis? Why have we suffered so many major humiliations like the September 18th Incident and the January 28th Incident and have no way to resist to the end with force? The root cause is all attributed to the failure of education. Because the past education cause was not well run, after decades of running new education, the result is not only unable to save China from the dangerous situation, but the danger is getting heavier day by day. This is obviously a failure of education. If we continue to muddle along for another five or ten years, I am afraid that the trend of international oppression will not allow us to wait peacefully for this long period. Naturally, we should quickly transform the education that is considered to have failed.

Under this major premise of requiring the transformation of education, many people have thought of transformation plans. The failure of past education is recognized by everyone, and the transformation plans are naturally different. For example, if someone has a very serious illness, they will definitely ask a doctor for diagnosis and treatment. Chinese medicine has its own medical methods, and Western medicine has its own medical methods. Similarly, Chinese or Western medicine may also have different medical methods. Therefore, under the major premise of transforming education, the plans put forward are also different. However, there is now an obvious common trend, which is that past education cannot create a group of students who can generate a kind of power after they graduate. What kind of power? That is the power to save themselves and save the country. In the past, students not only did not have the power to save the country, but they really did not even have the power to save themselves. Just looking at the so-called career movement of college graduates in Beijing, Tianjin, and parts of Shanghai this summer, we can expose that our education not only cannot enable students to have the power to save the country, but also cannot enable students to have the power to save themselves to find food. Therefore, the transformation of education should start from this place. How to make these students at least have the power of self-rescue first? If the power of self-rescue is really there, the power of saving the country will also follow. This kind of education that teaches students to save themselves and save the country is the road that future education must take, that is, production education or vocational education. Mr. Wu Zhihui recently wrote a long article in the Morning Post, saying that vocational education is really very good, but the Chinese people often disdain to listen to it. The term vocational education is considered not orthodox but a side branch, and most people despise it. It is better to call it "production education," and everyone may pay more attention to it. In short, regardless of vocational education or production education, people generally want to transform the education that used to specialize in writing articles, talking about law, and discussing social sciences, so that each student has the ability to produce. This kind of production capacity enables him to save himself and save the country after he leaves school in the future. Therefore, production education is a common trend in the transformation of education in the future. Now, from the central government to the provincial and municipal governments, to the people in the education circles, everyone believes that this major road of production education is the only one that should be taken in the future.

Baichuan Calligraphy and Painting Association Holds First Calligraphy and Painting Exhibition 215

Starting today at the Huzhou Society on Guizhou Road

Origin: In ancient times, calligraphy and painting had the same origin, used to replace language. Calligraphy has seal script and clerical script, and the brush has square and round shapes. As painting diverged, it was divided into the northern and southern schools. The northern school is close to science, and academy paintings mostly follow it. The southern school is close to philosophy, and it is not easy for non-scholars to create it. Since the Tang Dynasty used thirteen subjects to select scholars for painting, Tang Dynasty scholars, such as Han Changli and Du Shaoling, were unparalleled in poetry and prose and all understood painting. Wang Youcheng opened the southern school, using ink and wash method. The Yuan people followed it. Emperor Huizong of the Song Dynasty established a painting academy, specializing in proficiency. The northern school was at its peak, as for Ma Yuan and Xia Gui, the brush was simple and the meaning was ingenious, purely depicting real scenes. In the Ming Dynasty, painters were collected. In the early years of Hongwu, southern scholars were almost completely slaughtered, and Wu Wei was selected as the top painter. From then on, Jiang San Song, Guo Qing Kuang, and Zhang Ping Shan and his followers stirred up waves and adopted his techniques to make a name for themselves in the world. Those in the know called it wild fox meditation, and the northern school was swept away. Now, looking back on the past, tracing the source, not being surprised by the differences, hoping to reach the ultimate path. Yang Ziyun said, a hundred rivers study the sea, and when they reach the sea, they know what to choose, and can observe, without simply drawing oneself, one can achieve great success.

Evolution: This association aims to study calligraphy and painting, promote art, and promote culture. On November 15, 1933, Huang Binhong, Wang Jiyuan, Yan Kechang, Wu Mengfei, Liu Kang, Wang Yuanbo, Liang Shu, Zhang Xuan, Chen Renhao, Mo Yunxuan, Zhu Wenyun, and eleven other artists and scholars in Shanghai initiated the organization. Although art has myriad strands, its return is one. Just as a hundred rivers diverge and converge in the sea, dividing to the extreme is profound, but it must be united to achieve greatness. Therefore, it was named the Baichuan Calligraphy and Painting Association. It first gathered in the Huangshan Shuinan Shuangtang Painting Room in Shanghai and passed ten simple articles. It focused on practical research and discussion. It gathered once a week to study. Each member submitted several calligraphy and painting works for mutual evaluation and invited artists and scholars who were deeply knowledgeable in and out of the association to speak on the theory of calligraphy and painting, in order to achieve mutual learning. On March 6, 1934, the sixth research meeting was held. It was agreed that the membership of the association was gradually increasing and the organization should be meticulous. The simple articles of the association were considered too brief. It was resolved to revise them, and on March 12, the first members' congress was held at the Shanghai YMCA, and the constitution was revised and passed. The constitution consists of eight chapters and nineteen articles. According to the constitution, the first board of directors was elected, with Wang Jiyuan, Wu Mengfei, Huang Binhong, Zhu Wenyun, Wang Yuanbo, Yan Kechang, and Mo Yunxuan as directors. Wang Jiyuan was elected as the chairman. Since then, the organization of the association has gradually become complete. Although it has only been ten months, the membership has increased to more than 40 people, and the spirit of research is booming. On September 4, the second members' congress resolved to hold the first calligraphy and painting exhibition from October 3rd to 6th at the Shanghai Huzhou Society, for the appreciation of artists and scholars at home and abroad, and to promote the interest of colleagues in exploration.

Works by various artists: Wang Jiyuan, He Xiangning, Wang Yuanbo, Liang Kaishi, Wang Shengyuan, Wu Fuzhi, Wu Wenzhi, Yu Jingzhi, Liu Yazi, Yu Jianhua, Lang Bolong, Hu Youge, Ma Gongyu, Xu Peiji, Xu Zhengbai, Chen Renhao, Cao Yunzhong, Huang Binhong, Zhang Yiping, Zhang Chenbo, Zhang Xuan, Zhang Tianqi, Mo Yunxuan, Yan Kechang, Zhu Wenyun, Zhu Lesan, Liu Hairuo, Liu Shuxun, Liu Haisu, Pan Tianshou, Liu Kang, Xie Gongzhan. The works of the supporters include Lin Yuchao, Wang Yiting, Ju Juesheng, Ye Yufu, Cai Yuanpei and others.

Opening Dates: October 3rd to 6th, 9:00 AM to 5:00 PM daily.

World-Renowned Tennis Player Pan Lai Remains an Amateur 217

Three Major Reasons

The world's top amateur tennis player, Englishman Pan Lai, has maintained his amateur status and has not yet turned professional. According to his own account, there are three reasons: 1. The British government will extract half of his professional income as tax; 2. The British General Association and senior figures will no longer treat him as a noble guest, but will regard him as an ordinary performer; 3. His lover does not approve. Therefore, due to various losses, Pan Lai resolutely refused the offer of 50,000 yuan and said, "Please tell the world for me, Pan Lai is not happy about this."

Free Talk

On Advocating Science and Engineering 226

— Wang Pingling

If one is worthy of being called a modern Chinese, who would dare to defy the great trend of the world and express disagreement with advocating science and engineering! Novelists and playwrights are all people who need to enjoy modern life, and they will never raise the banner of rebellion against science and engineering again. If the value of novels and dramas is really just a kind of leisure toy, then in countries where science and engineering are not developed, there is not even the minimum resource for life, so where can there be the spare energy and leisure to spend on toys! According to this, the enthusiasm of literary figures for expecting the development of science and engineering should be more urgent than anyone else. If it is really because literature is too rampant that it has dragged down the decline of science and engineering in China, then as long as the gentlemen in China who study science and engineering can stand up and responsibly say, "China can stop buying foreign goods within a few years, and can stop hiring foreigners as engineers within a few years." I believe that in order to entrust their lives to the gifts of scientists and craftsmen, all those engaged in literary work will certainly be willing to obey their orders within the specified time limit, automatically put down their pens, and wait for the development of science and engineering. If there are also literary workers who can help them cheer and wave the flag for them, they will be happy to serve as long as they order.

I only hope that the reason for the decline of science and engineering in China is indeed so simple! I definitely do not hope that the decline of science and engineering in China has more complicated reasons than this. In order to advocate science and engineering, it is only necessary to shut down one or two literary publications and two or three literary newspaper sections, isn't it easy?

Literature is something that is unfathomable in its profundity, and the criteria for good and bad are like the market price in the morning and evening, making people uncertain. Therefore, some people spend their whole lives studying literature and have no hope for their whole lives, but only waste precious time and energy. It is truly a dead end and meaningless for a young man to fail in learning calligraphy, then learn swordsmanship, and then study literature. I believe that literature is something that one only studies when one is happy to study it. It is simply tyrannical to force someone who is not interested in literature to study literature. People can reluctantly study science and engineering and succeed, but they can never reluctantly study literature and become a literary figure, because literature cannot be learned. Very few of the world's great literary figures come from literature departments; George Bernard Shaw, Romain Rolland, and Maxim Gorky did not receive sufficient education. During the Qing Dynasty, scholars were selected solely on the basis of literature, but not a single literary figure was produced; and Cao Xueqin and Shi Nai'an were not known to have prominent academic titles. Therefore, shutting down literature departments may not be destroying literature, and establishing many literature departments may not be advocating literature. Literature does not need to be advocated, and advocating it is only like this; literature does not need to be cursed, and cursing it will not be like that. In fact, there is absolutely no such thing as everyone going to study literature. I do not believe at all that this useless literature can have such a great bad influence that it can drag down the decline of science and engineering in China! If it is said that the decline of science and engineering in China is entirely influenced by literature, then literature is too highly regarded. I dare to assert that there must be other more important reasons for the decline of science and engineering in China.

Before the revolution, although China's education system inevitably had the drawback of being impractical, there were special schools in each province for agriculture, forestry, animal husbandry, mining, railways, textiles, and medicine, etc., and universities had special departments. At least, the majority of students sent abroad by the national treasury every year studied science and engineering. Why are these experts with skills unable to do anything after they leave school and return to the country? One reason is that the government before the revolution did not take responsibility for allocating and regulating, leaving room for talents to develop adequately; the other reason is that the people were unwilling to invest in setting up factories, helping experts to have the possibility of testing their ambitions. Among them, there was no lack of experts who were determined to engage in science and engineering and did their best to set up a small-scale factory; but the Chinese only allow success and do not allow failure. Most of these people suffer a setback and are unable to recover. In the end, they either become depressed and fall into decline, or they completely abandon what they have learned and seek other ways of life. There are such examples in society, and those who come later no longer have the courage to continue trying. Therefore, those with better opportunities join the political world and become scientific officials who can also be regarded as specialized; those who are less capable mix in schools and become science teachers; the most unlucky ones can only wander in the attics like ordinary boring literati, specializing in writing scientific foreign stereotypes and exchanging foreign royalties for a living. In this situation, how can the future of science and engineering in China have any hope of being promoted! I pray that Mr. Wu, who advocates science and engineering, will write more articles in this area, urging the young people who are studying science and engineering today not to follow the mistakes of the past, immediately initiate national salvation savings, open several small-scale factories, and invite the experts who study science and engineering to come out and show the goods to the people. I hope that in the near future, there will be a "paper mill" and a "woolen mill" appearing. If someone properly initiates this matter, I will definitely pawn my pants to acknowledge a share and allow the experts in charge to have three consecutive opportunities to fail. As for the relationship between science and engineering and literature, it is still inevitably a "hypothetical question." Although it is said logically, we always feel that it is irrelevant.

Autumn in the Old Capital 227

— Zigang

Water chestnuts, withered lotus, red dates.

In Beiping, these three embellishments are indispensable in autumn. On the streets and alleys and in tea houses, vendors shout loudly with their ears covered. They carry a pair of water chestnut scissors and, when a transaction is made, "neatly" cut the water chestnuts, pad them with lotus leaves, and hand them to you. When your own lotus flower vat is empty, you can still see half a pond of withered lotus leaves in Beihai Park. Someone trims them, fearing that the yellowed and defeated leaves will drag away time. Long dates, round dates, and sour dates slowly turn red on the trees. Sometimes they are beaten down by people before they turn red. Green dates have no insects, and few good dates fall naturally. Especially the children of Beiping, if they do not have date trees in their own homes in autumn, they look forward to whose low wall or broken wall will have date branches hanging outwards. Then the bamboo poles rustle, and the children eat and have fun. The small date trees growing out of the cracks in the city walls are enough to be taken seriously. However, the harvest that takes more effort is sweeter. People are busy with nothing to do when they are idle.

There are fewer tourists in the park, and the tea houses are empty, but there are many people strolling back and forth. These are people who really come to take a walk. Often, the people who come to the tea houses in summer to drink tea are just joining in the fun, in order to see other people's elegance and let others see their own leisure. This is considered strolling.

Instead, the business of movie theaters and theaters is booming again. The scorching summer makes people stay indoors because of the smell of carbonic acid gas and sweat. In autumn, however, they are resurrected. Famous actors put on great plays, and tickets are always sold out for more than half a week in advance. Don't be surprised that there are so many theatergoers in Beiping, because people in all walks of life in Beiping are addicted to opera. Rickshaw drivers will come for two segments while waiting for business at night, facing the buildings where their masters are enjoying themselves. Students and even professors are all theater customers. This is called "Jingban" opera howling!

People say that Southerners like to eat, but why is Beiping any different? The fat crabs in autumn tempt people in the vegetable market. The newspapers publish advertisements for "newly arrived big crabs" from restaurants. Only the masters who don't count money go there, because they cost three or four mao each. Most people buy them home to cook themselves.

Mutton sells better than pork in Beiping, especially in autumn in three ways of eating: hot pot, barbecue, and stir-fry. There are particularly famous old shops, but almost every restaurant has them. Eating them hot with shallot sauce, garlic, and other ingredients is really a different kind of flavor. This is a very flavorful embellishment in Beiping. When the time comes, eating mutton with grandmothers and nephews is taken very seriously.

The Mid-Autumn Festival is indispensable for Rabbit God and mooncakes. Rabbit God has also been improved, with some sitting in cars and some sitting in airplanes, becoming modern. However, that stupid look cannot be changed, and people still find it fresh. Chestnuts are also cheap, 1.2 mao per catty. By the end of the year, they can be as cheap as 5 or 6 fen per catty. People can't forget the "festival."

The number of people who are quietly worrying about autumn is a hundred times greater than the number of people who smile comfortably. With the first autumn wind, people remember the winter's cold, and coal and winter clothes are all problems. The people who have sent winter clothes into the high walls are calculating how to get them out.

Small Talk Among the Eaves 228

— Leng Mo

Three: The Fated Drift

Those who are used to seeing stars all know how small the moon is, because it often passes between stars that are only two or three degrees apart, with plenty of room. And the distance of two or three degrees between two stars has always been seen as very short. The moon passing between the stars is one of the beautiful phenomena in the sky, but this can only be seen clearly during the new moon and waning moon, so those who look at the stars are not as interested in the full moon as ordinary people. The particularly bright full moon in autumn nights drowns out the Milky Way and most of the stars, which can almost be considered a hateful thing. Having only the moon and no stars makes the sky lose most of its interest. Ordinary people look at the moon and also hope for some wisps of cloud, forming a "cloud-backed moon," and if it is really clear to ten thousand miles without a cloud, they would find it monotonous. Usually, the moon seems static, but borrowing clouds can make it seem to move, which is even more lively. Those who know the stars see the moon as moving, and the stars are not easily grasped when they are not visible, while the moon seems to be stationary on the celestial sphere, turning with the sky.

Fortunately, the light of the full moon does not obscure stars of the second magnitude or higher. So the remaining countable ones! Are roughly all below the number that can be counted in one breath. Stars can still be used as markers. For example, this time, on the eve of the Mid-Autumn Festival, I saw the moon west of the Shi constellation, but on the night of the Mid-Autumn Festival, I saw it east of the Shi constellation. Now, in these two constellations Shi and Bi—these two constellations are the large quadrilateral in the sky. Looking due east after dark, almost anyone can recognize them—we can see the distance between them and the moon every night, which is very pleasing. The moon returns to the Shi constellation about every 27 days, which is a week of its journey in the sky.

We should consider it pleasant that he travels around like this. The Western moon goddess is fond of travel, but this fondness probably arose in the hunting era, so she only wanders in the forests. The Chinese moon goddess, after the autocratic system, has changed her nature. She is a rich and noble immortal who lives in a different residence every day. The so-called constellations (宿), are the meaning of residence (宿所). It is certainly unreasonable to still pronounce it as xiu (秀) now. The twenty-eight constellations are the daily residences of her journey for more than twenty-seven days. The old calendars now still note things like "Fire Room Build" (火房建) every day. The room (房) in it originally meant the constellation where the moon was located, but unfortunately, because of the difference between two sevens plus one-third and two eights, it is no longer accurate. However, based on what is noted on August 15th of this year, adding nine constellations, and then adding one constellation every three cycles, it can still be roughly accurate. This not only increases our interest in looking at the moon, but also allows us to recognize the twenty-eight constellations.

No matter how people set down the daily residences for the moon, the moon's circumnavigation is ultimately nothing more than drifting. The route of the residences is fixed, but her journey sometimes goes up and sometimes down, and her phases do not correspond to a week. Using astronomical explanations, of course, everything can be explained logically, but even if we know all that, it only makes us feel that her drifting is originally fated.

Not only these actions with known laws are completely fated, but also the moon's actions that are not yet clear may gradually escape the Earth's gravity and fly elsewhere; or it may gradually increase in weight and get closer to the Earth; or it may be swept away by unknown forces. No matter which it encounters, it is still fated. We will be able to measure that the moon has a destiny, but I don't know if the moon knows it. Like humans who are not very willing to admit their own destiny, she probably doesn't know either.

Welcome to the "Translation" Monthly 229

— Yuan Che

Previously, I once revealed "Hope" in this newspaper, saying, "We, a group of young people who are not very familiar with foreign languages but are seeking foreign heritage to engage in writing, cannot help but thank the translators of the past decade. Therefore, at present, I do not expect great creations to be produced, but I eagerly hope that more foreign literary masterpieces will be translated over." Therefore, recently seeing the appearance of the "Translation" Monthly (the first issue was published by Life Bookstore on September 16th), I personally not only feel very welcome, like "a baby lacking breast milk" once getting a wet nurse, but I also dare to raise my hands presumptuously and express a warm welcome on behalf of the young people who study literature like me.

Although, according to the "Preface" of the "Translation" Monthly, the translators "only occasionally read foreign works and translate them on a whim" and print them "as a reference for people who like to read translations"; they are not willing to deliberately and grandly raise the banner of translation, operate a company that transplants foreign literary heritage, and breastfeed us infants "who often cry in hunger in the slums." However, I want to say that after only reading the first issue, I personally have always felt like I have drunk a full meal of nutritious milk. Because this newly opened shop, under the honest signboard of "I am confident that I will not be sloppy," also features several old technicians who have refined good foreign milk for us to eat for the past decade. Although some of them are wearing different clothes than before, making us afraid to nod and greet them for a while, after drinking it, we immediately understand.

I think there must be many young people who feel the same as me. I hope that this new shop will open on time and expand its business (publishing series) so that the hands we have raised enthusiastically will not fall down coldly.

This is a hope realized, followed by another hope.

Village Head Mr. (17) 231

— Wang Renshu

"She...she went to call them." Mr. Feng Wen muttered, pacing around the room like a headless fly, then went out. After going out, he returned, arguing with Dong Sheng.

"I've said it already, there's no way, no way."

"You just say the easy things. Saying there's no way, is that the end of it?"

"If it's not the end, what can be done... I can't hold onto other people's feet…"

"What happens if you can't hold onto their feet?" Mr. Da Sheng continued. Dong Sheng waved his ginger-like hand, limping, into the dark room. Seeing the small room crowded with people wearing orange exercise uniforms, he was stunned, unable to speak for a moment.

"Ru Tong's father… Ru Tong's father, come and take a look!" Just as the two of them were at a loss for words, a woman's voice suddenly came from the kitchen.

Mr. Feng Wen started pacing around the room again.

"Go, your wife is calling you!" Mr. Da Sheng, knowing the reason for Mr. Feng Wen's embarrassment, said, "Anything you need, go to my shop assistant, and we can settle the accounts later. The squad leaders need supplies, you have to prepare them first."

"Then, brother Da Sheng, I'm leaving everything here to you, everything to you." At this moment, Mr. Feng Wen felt that being the village head was not something anyone could do! Attention! Present arms! Present your mother! Present what the hell?

"You tell me, why do you say there's no way?"

Dong Sheng, who had been stunned in front of the squad leaders and those in orange exercise uniforms, stood in a corner under the black ledger table, as if he had lost his breath. He was afraid that "锡茄烟" (a type of cigarette) and "洋火腿" (foreign ham) would be sent over again, so he was dazed. When Mr. Da Sheng asked him, he finally woke up and responded with a few "Oh! Oh." Finally, he said tremblingly,

"Oh oh, I've been running for three days, and and and went around for three days, but no no no one else came to the door."

"Hmm!" Mr. Da Sheng frowned first, then lowered his chin. Then he saw the squad leader's eyes, green like a cat's eyes, shining sharply.

Factory Strip 5,000

The Central Mint's Review Committee No. 15 announced a bulletin a few days ago. The committee has appointed chemist Glader to sample them in accordance with the regulations. Its fineness and weight are in compliance with the silver standard currency coinage regulations. A certificate will be issued from (23) 03424 to (23) 04913, a total of 1,490 sheets. In addition, the type B factory strip (880 fineness) cast by the Central Mint in September, from No. 31318 to No. 36317, a total of 5,000, when its "calibration mark" was made, the chemist Glader appointed by the committee also "supervised the stamping" in accordance with the regulations, and the fineness and weight of each strip were listed and registered. In addition to being approved for separate shipment, a detailed table is attached and the bulletin is announced to all.

Grain Futures Wheat Continues to Decline 242

Large Discrepancy Between Highs and Lows in Two Months

Yesterday, the wheat futures market, after the opening in the morning and afternoon, the market for each month showed a downward trend that was difficult to reverse. The quoted price for foreign wheat showed continued declines in Chicago, about 8 or 9 jiao, and in Canada, a small 4 fen to 1 jiao or so. Therefore, after the opening, the market sentiment for each month showed a state of being swept away like leaves in a storm, weak and lifeless. It is found that although this situation is mostly affected by the decline in foreign wheat, the bleak domestic consumption is also the main reason for the market's heavy burden and difficulty in rebounding. Looking back at the highest record two months ago (i.e., August 8), the huge drop is enough for those operating inside and outside the industry to think carefully. Yesterday, the lowest price for this month was 3.28 yuan, which is a huge difference of 1.45 yuan from the highest price. Yesterday's lowest price for November was 3.36 yuan, which is a difference of 1.36 yuan from the highest price. The difference for November was 1.35 yuan, and the difference for December was 1.24 yuan. In less than two months, the difference in fluctuations has opened up new views since the exchange was established. It can be seen that the rise and fall of prices must be natural. All artificial creations are not what speculation should involve. The result of one day was a uniform heavy decline due to increased selling pressure and weak buying power. This month fell by 8 fen, November fell by 9 fen, December fell by 6 fen, January fell by 5 fen, and February fell by 1 jiao. Due to each factory not needing it, current wheat has not yet opened, it is said.

The continued decline in New York wheat prices for one day caused better buying, but the quantity was not large. The possibility of importing miscellaneous grains from abroad is still a force that influences prices.
